    <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Date format\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         dd mm yyyy (\n         <a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">\n          AD\n         </a>\n Turks and Caicos Islands">\n          Calling code\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Area_code_649" title="Area code 649">\n          +1\xe2\x80\x91649\n </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        Turks and Caicos Islands\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">\n            t\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r/: \'ur\' in \'fur\'">\n            \xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">\n            s\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n           <span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: \'a\' in \'face\'">\n            e\xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99/: \'a\' in \'about\'">\n            \xc9\x99\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">\n            s\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n           <span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: \'a\' in \'face\'">\n            e\xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n           <span title="/o\xca\x8a/: \'o\' in \'code\'">\n            o\xca\x8a\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">\n            s\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n           <span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: \'a\' in \'face\'">\n            e\xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x92/: \'o\' in \'body\'">\n            \xc9\x92\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">\n            s\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ), or\n       <b>\n        TCI\n       </b>\n       for short, are a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" title="British Overseas Territory">\n        British Overseas Territory\n       </a>\n       consisting of the larger\n       <b>\n        Caicos Islands\n       </b>\n       and smaller\n       <b>\n        Turks Islands\n       </b>\n       , two groups of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_island" title="Tropical island">\n        tropical islands\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_Archipelago" title="Lucayan Archipelago">\n        Lucayan Archipelago\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">\n        Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       and northern\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">\n        West Indies\n       </a>\n       . They are known primarily for tourism and as an\n       <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centre" title="Offshore financial centre">\n        offshore financial centre\n       </a>\n       . The resident population is 31,458 as of 2012\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_3-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-3">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       of whom 23,769 live on\n       <a href="/wiki/Providenciales" title="Providenciales">\n        Providenciales\n       </a>\n       in the Caicos Islands.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Turks and Caicos Islands lie southeast of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mayaguana" title="Mayaguana">\n        Mayaguana\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">\n        Bahamas\n       </a>\n       island chain and north of the island of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">\n        Hispaniola\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">\n        Haiti\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">\n        Dominican Republic\n       </a>\n       ) and the other\n       <a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">\n        Antilles\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">\n        archipelago\n       </a>\n       islands.\n       <a href="/wiki/Cockburn_Town" title="Cockburn Town">\n        Cockburn Town\n       </a>\n       , the capital since 1766, is situated on\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Turk_Island" title="Grand Turk Island">\n        Grand Turk Island\n       </a>\n       about 1,042 kilometres (647\xc2\xa0mi) east-southeast of\n       <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">\n        Miami\n       </a>\n       , United States. The islands have a total land area of 430 square kilometres (170\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-area_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-area-8">\n         [b]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first recorded European sighting of the islands now known as the Turks and Caicos occurred in 1512.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leon_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-leon-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the subsequent centuries, the islands were claimed by several European powers with the\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">\n        British Empire\n       </a>\n       eventually gaining control. For many years the islands were governed indirectly through\n       <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">\n        Bermuda\n       </a>\n       , the Bahamas, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">\n        Jamaica\n       </a>\n       . When the Bahamas gained independence in 1973, the islands received their\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Governor of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        own governor\n       </a>\n       , and have remained a separate autonomous\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" title="British Overseas Territory">\n        British Overseas Territory\n       </a>\n       since. In August 2009, the United Kingdom suspended the Turks and Caicos Islands\' self-government following allegations of ministerial corruption.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Home rule was restored in the islands after the\n       <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_general_election,_2012" title="Turks and Caicos Islands general election, 2012">\n        November 2012 elections\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div tocsection-40">\n           <a href="#sport">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             17.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             sport\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41">\n           <a href="#politics_2">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             17.2\n           Notes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           20\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45">\n         <a href="#Bibliography">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           21\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Bibliography\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           22\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">\n        Etymology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The Turks and Caicos Islands are named after the Turk\'s cap cactus (\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melocactus_intortus" title="Melocactus intortus">\n         Melocactus intortus\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ), and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">\n        Lucayan\n       </a>\n       term\n       <i>\n        caya hico\n       </i>\n       , meaning \'string of islands\'.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="History of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        History of the Turks and Caicos Islands\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The first inhabitants of the islands were\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawakan_language" title="Arawakan language">\n        Arawakan-speaking\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">\n        Ta\xc3\xadno people\n       </a>\n       , who crossed over from\n       <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">\n        Hispaniola\n       </a>\n       sometime from AD 500 to 800. Together with Taino who migrated from\n       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">\n        Cuba\n       </a>\n       to the southern Bahamas around the same time, these people developed as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_people" title="Lucayan people">\n        Lucayan\n       </a>\n       . Around 1200, the Turks and Caicos Islands were resettled by Classical Ta\xc3\xadnos from Hispaniola.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Soon after the Spanish arrived in the islands in 1512,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leon_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-leon-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       they began capturing the Ta\xc3\xadno of the Turks and Caicos Islands and the Lucayan as slaves (technically, as workers in the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">\n         encomienda\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       system)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       to replace the largely depleted native population of Hispaniola. The southern Bahama Islands and the Turks and Caicos Islands were completely depopulated by about 1513, and remained so until the 17th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first European documented to sight the islands was\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">\n        conquistador\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n">\n        Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n\n       </a>\n       , who did so in 1512.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leon_9-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-leon-9">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During the 16th, 17th, and 18th centuries, the islands passed from Spanish, to French, to\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">\n        British\n       </a>\n       control, but none of the three powers ever established any settlements.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement">\n        Settlement\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Settlement">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_raking_salt_stamp_1938.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="848" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_raking_salt_stamp_1938.jpg/220px-Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_raking_salt_stamp_1938.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_raking_salt_stamp_1938.jpg/330px-Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_raking_salt_stamp_1938.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_raking_salt_stamp_1938.jpg/440px-Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_raking_salt_stamp_1938.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_raking_salt_stamp_1938.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Raking salt on a 1938 postage stamp of the islands.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Bermudian salt collectors settled the Turks Islands around 1680. For several decades around the turn of the 18th century, the islands became popular\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pirate" title="Pirate">\n        pirate\n       </a>\n       hideouts. From 1765\xe2\x80\x931783, the islands were under French occupation, and again after the French\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grand_Turk" title="Battle of Grand Turk">\n        captured the archipelago\n       </a>\n       in 1783.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">\n        American War of Independence\n       </a>\n       (1775\xe2\x80\x931783), many\n       <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">\n        Loyalists\n       </a>\n       fled to British Caribbean colonies; in 1783, they were the first settlers on the Caicos Islands. They developed cotton as an important cash crop, but it was superseded by the development of the salt industry.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1799, both the Turks and the Caicos island groups were annexed by Britain as part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">\n        Bahamas\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The processing of sea salt was developed as a highly important export product from the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">\n        West Indies\n       </a>\n       , with the labour done by African slaves. Salt continued to be a major export product into the nineteenth century.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Lighthouse_Park_on_Grand_Turk.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Historic_Lighthouse_Park_on_Grand_Turk.jpg/220px-Historic_Lighthouse_Park_on_Grand_Turk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Historic_Lighthouse_Park_on_Grand_Turk.jpg/330px-Historic_Lighthouse_Park_on_Grand_Turk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Historic_Lighthouse_Park_on_Grand_Turk.jpg/440px-Historic_Lighthouse_Park_on_Grand_Turk.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Lighthouse_Park_on_Grand_Turk.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Grand_Turk_Lighthouse" title="Grand Turk Lighthouse">\n          1852 lighthouse on Grand Turk\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1807, Britain prohibited the slave trade and, in 1833, abolished slavery in its colonies. British ships sometimes intercepted slave traders in the Caribbean, and some ships were wrecked off the coast of these islands. In 1837, the\n       <i>\n        Esperanza,\n       </i>\n       a Portuguese slaver, was wrecked off East Caicos, one of the larger islands. While the crew and 220 captive Africans survived the shipwreck, 18 Africans died before the survivors were taken to Nassau. Africans from this ship may have been among the 189 liberated Africans whom the British colonists settled in the Turks and Caicos from 1833 to 1840.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadler210-212_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sadler210-212-20">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1841, the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Trouvadore" title="Trouvadore">\n         Trouvadore\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , an illegal Spanish slave ship, was wrecked off the coast of East Caicos. All the 20-man crew and 192 captive Africans survived the sinking. Officials freed the Africans and arranged for 168 persons to be\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apprenticed" title="Apprenticed">\n        apprenticed\n       </a>\n       to island proprietors on Grand Turk Island for one year. They increased the small population of the colony by seven percent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadler210-212_20-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sadler210-212-20">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Numerous descendants have come from those free Africans. The remaining 24 were resettled in\n       <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">\n        Nassau\n       </a>\n       . The Spanish crew were also taken there, to be turned over to the custody of the Cuban consul and taken to Cuba for prosecution.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sutton_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sutton-21">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An 1878 letter documents the "Trouvadore Africans" and their descendants as constituting an essential part of the "labouring population" on the islands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadler210-212_20-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sadler210-212-20">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2004, marine\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaeologists" title="Archaeologists">\n        archaeologists\n       </a>\n       affiliated with the Turks and Caicos National Museum discovered a wreck, called the "Black Rock Ship", that subsequent research has suggested may be that of the\n       <i>\n        Trouvadore\n       </i>\n       . In November 2008, a cooperative marine archaeology expedition, funded by the United States\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Oceanographic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanographic and Atmospheric Administration">\n        NOAA\n       </a>\n       , confirmed that the wreck has artefacts whose style and date of manufacture link them to the\n       <i>\n        Trouvadore\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sutton_21-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sutton-21">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadler_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sadler-23">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_reorganisation">\n        Political reorganisation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Political reorganisation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In 1848, Britain designated the Turks and Caicos as a separate colony under a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council_President_of_the_Turks_of_Caicos" title="Council President of the Turks of Caicos">\n        council president\n       </a>\n       . In 1873, the islands were made part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">\n        Jamaica\n       </a>\n       colony; in 1894, the chief colonial official was restyled\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commissioner_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Commissioner of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        commissioner\n       </a>\n       . In 1917, Canadian Prime Minister\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Borden" title="Robert Borden">\n        Robert Borden\n       </a>\n       suggested that the Turks and Caicos join Canada, but this suggestion was rejected by British Prime Minister\n       <a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_George" title="David Lloyd George">\n        David Lloyd George\n       </a>\n       . The islands remained a dependency of Jamaica.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 4 July 1959, the islands were again designated as a separate colony, the last commissioner being restyled\n       <a href="/wiki/Administrator_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos" title="Administrator of the Turks and Caicos">\n        administrator\n       </a>\n       . The governor of Jamaica also continued as the governor of the islands. When Jamaica was granted independence from Britain in August 1962, the Turks and Caicos Islands became a\n       <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">\n        Crown colony\n       </a>\n       . Beginning in 1965, the governor of the Bahamas also was governor of the Turks and Caicos Islands and oversaw affairs for the islands.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       When the Bahamas gained independence in 1973, the Turks and Caicos received their own governor (the last administrator was restyled). In 1974, Canadian\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party_(Canada)" title="New Democratic Party (Canada)">\n        New Democratic Party\n       </a>\n       MP\n       <a href="/wiki/Max_Saltsman" title="Max Saltsman">\n        Max Saltsman\n       </a>\n       tried to use his\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_Member%27s_Bill" title="Private Member\'s Bill">\n        Private Member\'s Bill\n       </a>\n       for legislation to annex the islands to Canada, but it did not pass in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_House_of_Commons" title="Canadian House of Commons">\n        Canadian House of Commons\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saltsman_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-saltsman-25">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since August 1976, the islands have had their own government headed by a chief minister (now premier), the first of whom was\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Alexander_George_Smith_McCartney" title="James Alexander George Smith McCartney">\n        James Alexander George Smith McCartney\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The islands\' political troubles in the early 21st century resulted in a rewritten\n       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands#2006" title="Constitution of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        constitution\n       </a>\n       promulgated in 2006. In 2009, after Premier\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Misick" title="Michael Misick">\n        Misick\n       </a>\n       resigned in the face of corruption charges, the United Kingdom took over direct control of the government.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A new\n       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands#2011" title="Constitution of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        constitution\n       </a>\n       was promulgated in October 2012 and the government was returned to local administration after the November 2012 elections.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clegg_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Clegg-27">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 2016 elections Rufus Ewing\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Progressive_National_Party_(Turks_and_Caicos_Islands)" title="Progressive National Party (Turks and Caicos Islands)">\n        Progressive National Party\n       </a>\n       (PNP) lost for the first time since they replaced\n       <a href="/wiki/Derek_Hugh_Taylor" title="Derek Hugh Taylor">\n        Taylor\'s\n       </a>\n       government in 2003. The\n       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Movement_(Turks_and_Caicos_Islands)" title="People\'s Democratic Movement (Turks and Caicos Islands)">\n        People\'s Democratic Movement\n       </a>\n       (PDM) came to power with\n       <a href="/wiki/Sharlene_Cartwright-Robinson" title="Sharlene Cartwright-Robinson">\n        Sharlene Cartwright-Robinson\n       </a>\n       as Premier.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-Top-jobs_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC-Top-jobs-28">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TurksandCaicosOMC.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="671" data-file-width="969" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/TurksandCaicosOMC.png/400px-TurksandCaicosOMC.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/TurksandCaicosOMC.png/600px-TurksandCaicosOMC.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/TurksandCaicosOMC.png/800px-TurksandCaicosOMC.png 2x" width="400"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TurksandCaicosOMC.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <center>\n          Map of the Turks and Caicos Islands.\n         </center>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The two island groups are in the North Atlantic Ocean, southeast of\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">\n        the Bahamas\n       </a>\n       , northwest of\n       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">\n        Puerto Rico\n       </a>\n       , north of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">\n        Hispaniola\n       </a>\n       , and about 1,000 kilometres (620\xc2\xa0mi) from Miami in the United States, at\n       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">\n        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;params=21_45_N_71_35_W_">\n         <span class="geo-default">\n          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">\n           <span class="latitude">\n            21\xc2\xb045\xe2\x80\xb2N\n           </span>\n           <span class="longitude">\n            71\xc2\xb035\xe2\x80\xb2W\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         <span class="geo-multi-punct">\n          \xef\xbb\xbf / \xef\xbb\xbf\n         </span>\n         <span class="geo-nondefault">\n          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">\n           21.750\xc2\xb0N 71.583\xc2\xb0W\n          </span>\n          <span style="display:none">\n           \xef\xbb\xbf /\n           <span class="geo">\n            21.750; -71.583\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       <span style="font-size: small;">\n        <span id="coordinates">\n         <a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">\n          Coordinates\n         </a>\n         :\n         <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">\n          <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;params=21_45_N_71_35_W_">\n           <span class="geo-default">\n            <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">\n             <span class="latitude">\n              21\xc2\xb045\xe2\x80\xb2N\n             </span>\n             <span class="longitude">\n              71\xc2\xb035\xe2\x80\xb2W\n             </span>\n            </span>\n           </span>\n           <span class="geo-multi-punct">\n            \xef\xbb\xbf / \xef\xbb\xbf\n           </span>\n           <span class="geo-nondefault">\n            <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">\n             21.750\xc2\xb0N 71.583\xc2\xb0W\n            </span>\n            <span style="display:none">\n             \xef\xbb\xbf /\n             <span class="geo">\n              21.750; -71.583\n             </span>\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       . The territory is\n       <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">\n        geographically\n       </a>\n       contiguous to the Bahamas, both comprising the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_Archipelago" title="Lucayan Archipelago">\n        Lucayan Archipelago\n       </a>\n       , but is politically a separate entity. The Caicos Islands are separated by the Caicos Passage from the closest Bahamian islands,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mayaguana" title="Mayaguana">\n        Mayaguana\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Inagua" title="Great Inagua">\n        Great Inagua\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The eight main islands and more than 299 smaller islands\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       have a total land area of 616.3 square kilometres (238.0 square miles),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-area_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-area-8">\n         [b]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       consisting primarily of low, flat\n       <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">\n        limestone\n       </a>\n       with extensive\n       <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">\n        marshes\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">\n        mangrove\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Swamp" title="Swamp">\n        swamps\n       </a>\n       and 332 square kilometres (128\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) of beach front. The weather is usually sunny (it is generally regarded that the islands receive 350 days of sun each year\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ) and relatively dry, but suffers frequent\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">\n        hurricanes\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       The islands have limited natural\n       <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">\n        fresh water\n       </a>\n       resources; private cisterns collect rainwater for drinking. The primary natural resources are\n       <a href="/wiki/Spiny_lobster" title="Spiny lobster">\n        spiny lobster\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Conch" title="Conch">\n        conch\n       </a>\n       , and other shellfish.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The two distinct island groups are separated by the Turks Islands Passage.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Turks_Islands">\n        Turks Islands\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Turks Islands">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Turks Islands are separated from the Caicos Islands by Turks Island Passage, which is more than 2,200\xc2\xa0m or 7,200\xc2\xa0ft deep,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The islands form a chain that stretches north\xe2\x80\x93south. The 2012 Census population was 4,939 on the two main islands, the only inhabited islands of the group:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Grand_Turk_Island" title="Grand Turk Island">\n         Grand Turk\n        </a>\n        (with the capital of the territory, area 17.39\xc2\xa0km\n        <sup>\n         2\n        </sup>\n        (6.71\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi),\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-depstc.org_31-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-depstc.org-31">\n          [29]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        population 4,831)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Salt_Cay,_Turks_Islands" title="Salt Cay, Turks Islands">\n         Salt Cay\n        </a>\n        (area 6.74\xc2\xa0km\n        <sup>\n         2\n        </sup>\n        (2.60\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi),\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-depstc.org_31-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-depstc.org-31">\n          [29]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        population 108)\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Together with nearby islands, all on Turks Bank, those two main islands form two of the six administrative\n       <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Districts of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        districts\n       </a>\n       of the territory that fall within the Turks Islands. Turks Bank, which is smaller than Caicos Bank, has a total area of about 324\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       (125\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seaaroundus.org_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-seaaroundus.org-32">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mouchoir_Bank">\n        Mouchoir Bank\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mouchoir Bank">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       25 kilometres (16\xc2\xa0mi) east of the Turks Islands and separated from them by Mouchoir Passage is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mouchoir_Bank" title="Mouchoir Bank">\n        Mouchoir Bank\n       </a>\n       . Although it has no emergent cays or islets, some parts are very shallow and the water breaks on them. Mouchoir Bank is part of the Turks and Caicos Islands and falls within its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">\n        Exclusive Economic Zone\n       </a>\n       . It measures 960 square kilometres (370\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) in area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Two banks further east,\n       <a href="/wiki/Silver_Bank" title="Silver Bank">\n        Silver Bank\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Navidad_Bank" title="Navidad Bank">\n        Navidad Bank\n       </a>\n       , are geographically a continuation, but belong politically to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">\n        Dominican Republic\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Caicos_Islands">\n        Caicos Islands\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Caicos Islands">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The largest island in the Caicos archipelago is the sparsely-inhabited Middle Caicos, which measures 144 square kilometres (56\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) in area, but has a population of only 168 at the 2012 Census. The most populated island is\n       <a href="/wiki/Providenciales" title="Providenciales">\n        Providenciales\n       </a>\n       , with 23,769 inhabitants in 2012, and an area of 122 square kilometres (47\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi).\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Caicos" title="North Caicos">\n        North Caicos\n       </a>\n       (116 square kilometres (45\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) in area) had 1,312 inhabitants.\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Caicos" title="South Caicos">\n        South Caicos\n       </a>\n       (21 square kilometres (8.1\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) in area) had 1,139 inhabitants, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Parrot_Cay" title="Parrot Cay">\n        Parrot Cay\n       </a>\n       (6 square kilometres (2.3\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) in area) had 131 inhabitants.\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Caicos" title="East Caicos">\n        East Caicos\n       </a>\n       (which is administered as part of South Caicos District) is uninhabited, while the only permanent inhabitants of\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Caicos" title="West Caicos">\n        West Caicos\n       </a>\n       (administered as part of Providenciales District) are resort staff.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The Turks and Caicos Islands feature tropical climate, with relatively consistent temperatures throughout the course of the year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Summertime temperatures rarely exceed 33\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (91\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) and winter nighttime temperatures rarely fall below 18\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (64\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F).\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <table class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n          <a href="#cite_note-36">\n           [34]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">\n        Politics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Politics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cockburn_Town.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="811" data-file-width="1460" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Cockburn_Town.jpg/220px-Cockburn_Town.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Cockburn_Town.jpg/330px-Cockburn_Town.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Cockburn_Town.jpg/440px-Cockburn_Town.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cockburn_Town.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A street in\n         <a href="/wiki/Cockburn_Town" title="Cockburn Town">\n          Cockburn Town\n         </a>\n         , the capital of the Turks and Caicos Islands\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1358" data-file-width="2206" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/220px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/330px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map of the European Union in the world with overseas countries and territories and outermost regions\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Politics of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        Politics of the Turks and Caicos Islands\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Turks and Caicos Islands are a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" title="British Overseas Territory">\n        British Overseas Territory\n       </a>\n       . As a British territory, its sovereign is Queen\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">\n        Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom\n       </a>\n       , represented by a\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Governor of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        governor\n       </a>\n       appointed by the monarch, on the advice of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_Office" title="Foreign Office">\n        Foreign Office\n       </a>\n       . The United Nations\n       <a href="/wiki/Special_Committee_on_Decolonization" title="Special Committee on Decolonization">\n        Special Committee on Decolonization\n       </a>\n       includes the territory on the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">\n        United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With the election of the territory\'s first Chief Minister,\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Alexander_George_Smith_McCartney" title="James Alexander George Smith McCartney">\n        J.A.G.S. McCartney\n       </a>\n       , the islands adopted a constitution on 30 August 1976, which is Constitution Day, the national holiday.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Constitutional_suspension_(1986\xe2\x80\x931988)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutional_suspension_.281986.E2.80.931988.29">\n        Constitutional suspension (1986\xe2\x80\x931988)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Constitutional suspension (1986\xe2\x80\x931988)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The constitution was suspended in 1986, but restored and revised 5 March 1988. In the interim two Advisory Councils took over with members from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Progressive_National_Party_(Turks_and_Caicos_Islands)" title="Progressive National Party (Turks and Caicos Islands)">\n        Progressive National Party\n       </a>\n       (PNP),\n       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Movement_(Turks_and_Caicos_Islands)" title="People\'s Democratic Movement (Turks and Caicos Islands)">\n        People\'s Democratic Movement\n       </a>\n       (PDM) and\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=National_Democratic_Alliance_(Turks_and_Caicos_Islands)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="National Democratic Alliance (Turks and Caicos Islands) (page does not exist)">\n        National Democratic Alliance\n       </a>\n       (NDA), which was a splinter group from the PNP:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        1st Council (1986\xe2\x80\x931987)\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Misick" title="Ariel Misick">\n           Ariel Misick\n          </a>\n          (NDA) \xe2\x80\x93 also served as minister of development and commerce\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Misick" title="Emmanuel Misick">\n           Emmanuel Misick\n          </a>\n          (NDA)\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Clement_Howell" title="Clement Howell">\n           Clement Howell\n          </a>\n          (PDM)\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Simons" title="Carlos Simons">\n           Carlos Simons\n          </a>\n          (NDA)\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Elliot Williams (PDM) \xe2\x80\x93 Indigenous Liaison Officer and former Mayor of\n          <a href="/wiki/Cockburn_Town" title="Cockburn Town">\n           Cockburn Town\n          </a>\n          .\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2nd Council (1987\xe2\x80\x931988)\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Malcolm" title="Daniel Malcolm">\n           Daniel Malcolm\n          </a>\n          (PNP) \xe2\x80\x93 former leader of PNP\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tom_Lightbourne&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tom Lightbourne (page does not exist)">\n           Tom Lightbourne\n          </a>\n          (PNP) \xe2\x80\x93 Chairman of PNP\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Herbie_Ingham&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Herbie Ingham (page does not exist)">\n           Herbie Ingham\n          </a>\n          (NDA) \xe2\x80\x93 later as\n          <a href="/wiki/Providenciales_International_Airport" title="Providenciales International Airport">\n           Providenciales International Airport\n          </a>\n          Authority Chairman\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution_2006">\n        Constitution 2006\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Constitution 2006">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       A new constitution came into force on 9 August 2006, but was in parts suspended and amended in 2009. The territory\'s legal system is based on\n       <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">\n        English\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">\n        common law\n       </a>\n       , with a small number of laws adopted from\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">\n        Jamaica\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">\n        Bahamas\n       </a>\n       . Suffrage is universal for those over 18 years of age. English is the official language.\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Turk_Island" title="Grand Turk Island">\n        Grand Turk\n       </a>\n       is the administrative and political capital of the Turks and Caicos Islands and Cockburn Town has been the seat of government since 1766.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Under the suspended 2006 constitution, the head of government was the\n       <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Premier of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        premier\n       </a>\n       , filled by the leader of the elected party. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Cabinet of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        cabinet\n       </a>\n       consisted of three\n       <a href="/wiki/Ex_officio_member" title="Ex officio member">\n        <i>\n         ex officio\n        </i>\n        members\n       </a>\n       and five appointed by the governor from among the members of the House of Assembly. The unicameral\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_House_of_Assembly" title="Turks and Caicos Islands House of Assembly">\n        House of Assembly\n       </a>\n       consisted of 21 seats, of which 15 were popularly elected; members serve four-year terms.\n       <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Elections in the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        Elections in the Turks and Caicos Islands\n       </a>\n       were\n       <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_general_election,_2003" title="Turks and Caicos Islands general election, 2003">\n        held\n       </a>\n       on 24 April 2003 and\n       <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_general_election,_2007" title="Turks and Caicos Islands general election, 2007">\n        again\n       </a>\n       on 9 February 2007. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Progressive_National_Party_(Turks_and_Caicos_Islands)" title="Progressive National Party (Turks and Caicos Islands)">\n        Progressive National Party\n       </a>\n       , led by Michael Misick, held thirteen seats, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Movement_(Turks_and_Caicos_Islands)" title="People\'s Democratic Movement (Turks and Caicos Islands)">\n        People\'s Democratic Movement\n       </a>\n       , led by Floyd Seymour, held two seats.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Under the new constitution that came into effect in October 2012, legislative power is held by a unicameral House of Assembly, consisting of 19 seats, 15 elected and 4 appointed by the governor; of elected members, five are elected at large and 10 from single member districts for four-year terms. After the 2012 elections,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rufus_Ewing" title="Rufus Ewing">\n        Rufus Ewing\n       </a>\n       of the Progressive National Party won a narrow majority of the elected seats and was appointed premier.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Turks and Caicos Islands participates in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Development_Bank" title="Caribbean Development Bank">\n        Caribbean Development Bank\n       </a>\n       , is an associate in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CARICOM" title="CARICOM">\n        CARICOM\n       </a>\n       , member of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Universal_Postal_Union" title="Universal Postal Union">\n        Universal Postal Union\n       </a>\n       and maintains an\n       <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">\n        Interpol\n       </a>\n       sub-bureau. Defence is the responsibility of the United Kingdom.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_proposal">\n        Independence proposal\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Independence proposal">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The winning party of Turks and Caicos\' first general election in 1976, the People\'s Democratic Movement (PDM) under\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Alexander_George_Smith_McCartney" title="James Alexander George Smith McCartney">\n        "Jags" McCartney\n       </a>\n       , sought to establish a framework and accompanying infrastructure in the pursuit of an eventual policy of full independence for the islands. However, with the early death of McCartney, confidence in the country\'s leadership waned. In 1980, the PDM agreed with the British government that independence would be granted in 1982 if the PDM was re-elected in the elections of that year.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       That election was effectively a referendum on the independence issue and was won by the pro-dependency Progressive National Party (PNP), which claimed victory again four years later. With these developments, the independence issue largely faded from the political scene.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       However, in the mid-2000s, the issue of independence for the islands was again raised. In April 2006, PNP Premier\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Misick" title="Michael Misick">\n        Michael Misick\n       </a>\n       reaffirmed that his party saw independence from Britain as the "ultimate goal" for the islands, but not at the present time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2008, opponents of Misick accused him of moving toward independence for the islands to dodge a commission of inquiry, which examined reports of corruption by the Misick Administration.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">\n        Administrative divisions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Districts of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        Districts of the Turks and Caicos Islands\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Turks and Caicos Islands are divided into six administrative districts (two in the Turks Islands and four in the Caicos Islands), headed by district commissioners. For the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_House_of_Assembly" title="Turks and Caicos Islands House of Assembly">\n        House of Assembly\n       </a>\n       , the Turks and Caicos Islands are divided into 15 electoral districts (four in the Turks Islands and eleven in the Caicos Islands).\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption_scandal_and_suspension_of_self-government">\n        Corruption scandal and suspension of self-government\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Corruption scandal and suspension of self-government">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Background">\n        Background\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Background">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       In 2008, after members of the British parliament conducting a routine review of the administration received several reports of high-level official corruption in the Turks and Caicos,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       then-Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Tauwhare" title="Richard Tauwhare">\n        Richard Tauwhare\n       </a>\n       announced the appointment of a Commission of Enquiry into corruption.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The same year, Premier\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Misick" title="Michael Misick">\n        Michael Misick\n       </a>\n       himself became the focus of a criminal investigation after a woman identified by news outlets as an American citizen residing in Puerto Rico accused him of sexually assaulting her,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       although he strongly denies the charge.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On Monday, 16 March 2009, the UK threatened to suspend self-government in the islands and transfer power to the new governor,\n       <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Wetherell" title="Gordon Wetherell">\n        Gordon Wetherell\n       </a>\n       , over\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Systemic_corruption" title="Systemic corruption">\n        systemic corruption\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-UKAction_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC-UKAction-45">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 18 March 2009, on the advice of her UK ministers,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" title="Queen Elizabeth II">\n        Queen Elizabeth II\n       </a>\n       issued an\n       <a href="/wiki/Order_in_Council" title="Order in Council">\n        Order in Council\n       </a>\n       giving the Governor the power to suspend those parts of the 2006 Constitution that deal with ministerial government and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_House_of_Assembly" title="Turks and Caicos Islands House of Assembly">\n        House of Assembly\n       </a>\n       , and to exercise the powers of government himself. The order, which would also establish an Advisory Council and Consultative Forum in place of the House of Assembly, would come into force on a date to be announced by the governor, and remain in force for two years unless extended or revoked.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 23 March 2009, after the enquiry found evidence of "high probability of systemic corruption or other serious dishonesty", Misick resigned as Premier to make way for a new, unified government.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP-PMquits_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AFP-PMquits-47">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Politicians were accused of selling crown land for personal gain and misusing public funds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Times-48">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The following day,\n       <a href="/wiki/Galmo_Williams" title="Galmo Williams">\n        Galmo Williams\n       </a>\n       was sworn in as his replacement.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP-PMquits_47-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AFP-PMquits-47">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FP-WilliamsSworn_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FP-WilliamsSworn-49">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Misick denied all charges, and referred to the British government\'s debate on whether to remove the territory\'s sovereignty as "tantamount to being re-colonised. It is a backwards step completely contrary to the whole movement of history."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_48-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Times-48">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Suspension_and_reactions">\n        Suspension and reactions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Suspension and reactions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       On 14 August 2009 after Misick\'s last appeals failed, the Governor, on the instructions of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">\n        Foreign and Commonwealth Office\n       </a>\n       , imposed direct rule on the Turks and Caicos Islands by authority of the 18 March 2009\n       <a href="/wiki/Order_in_Council" title="Order in Council">\n        Order in Council\n       </a>\n       issued by the Queen. The islands\' administration was suspended for up to two years, with possible extensions, and power was transferred to the Governor, with the United Kingdom also stationing a supply vessel in between Turks and Caicos.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Under-Secretary_of_State_for_Foreign_Affairs" title="Parliamentary Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs">\n        Parliamentary Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Chris_Bryant" title="Chris Bryant">\n        Chris Bryant\n       </a>\n       said of the decision to impose rule, "This is a serious constitutional step which the UK Government has not taken lightly but these measures are essential in order to restore good governance and sound financial management."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indep_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Indep-50">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The move was met with vehement opposition by the former Turks and Caicos government, with Misick\'s successor Williams calling it a "\n       <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d\'\xc3\xa9tat">\n        coup\n       </a>\n       ", and stating that, "Our country is being invaded and re-\n       <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">\n        colonised\n       </a>\n       by the United Kingdom, dismantling a duly elected government and legislature and replacing it with a one-man\n       <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">\n        dictatorship\n       </a>\n       , akin to that of the old Red China, all in the name of good governance."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indep_50-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Indep-50">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Despite this, the civilian populace was reported to be largely welcoming of the enforced rule.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indep_50-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Indep-50">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The British government stated that they intended to keep true to their word that the country would regain home rule in two years or less, and Foreign Office Minister Chris Bryant said that elections would be held in 2011, "or sooner".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FT_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FT-51">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Governor Wetherell stated that he would aim to "make a clean break from the mistakes of the past" and create "a durable path towards good governance, sound financial management and sustainable development". Wetherell added: "In the meantime we must all learn to foster a quality of public spirit, listen to all those who have the long-term interests of these islands at heart, and safeguard the fundamental assets of the Territory for future generations... Our guiding principles will be those of transparency, accountability and responsibility. I believe that most people in the Turks and Caicos will welcome these changes."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indep_50-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Indep-50">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="New_government_formed">\n        New government formed\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: New government formed">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       On 12 June 2012 British\n       <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Affairs" title="Secretary of State for Foreign and Commonwealth Affairs">\n        Foreign Secretary\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Hague" title="William Hague">\n        William Hague\n       </a>\n       announced that fresh elections would be held in November 2012, stating that there had been "significant progress with an ambitious reform programme" and that there had been "sufficient progress, on the milestones and on putting in place robust financial controls"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCO_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FCO-52">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A new\n       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Constitution of the Turks and Caicos Islands">\n        constitution\n       </a>\n       was approved on 15 October 2012. The terms of the election are specified in the constitution.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">\n        Judiciary\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Judiciary">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The judicial branch of government is headed by a Supreme Court; appeals are heard by the Court of Appeal and final appeals by the United Kingdom\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">\n        Judicial Committee of the Privy Council\n       </a>\n       . There are three justices of the Supreme Court, a Chief Justice and two others. The Court of Appeal consists of a president and at least two justices of appeal.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Magistrates\' Courts are the lower courts and appeals from Magistrates\' Courts are sent to the Supreme Court.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of September 2014, the Chief Justice is Justice Margaret Ramsay-Hale.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Chief Justices\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        John Charles Powell Fieldsend 1985\xe2\x80\x931987\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Smith_(barrister)" title="Frederick Smith (barrister)">\n         Sir Frederick Smith\n        </a>\n        1987\xe2\x80\x931990\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Lindsey Worrall 1990\xe2\x80\x931993\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Kipling Douglas 1993\xe2\x80\x931996\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Sir\n        <a href="/wiki/Richard_Ground" title="Richard Ground">\n         Richard Ground\n        </a>\n        1998\xe2\x80\x932004\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Christopher Gardner 2004\xe2\x80\x932007\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Sir\n        <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Ward" title="Gordon Ward">\n         Gordon Ward\n        </a>\n        2008\xe2\x80\x932012\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Edwin Goldsbrough 2012\xe2\x80\x932014\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Margaret Ramsey Hale 2014\xe2\x80\x93present\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Population">\n        Population\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Population">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0 0 1em 1em;">\n       <tr>\n        <th style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\n         20,014\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\n         +74.6%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">\n         2012\n        </th>\n        <td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\n         31,458\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\n         +57.2%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">\n         Source:\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcweeklynews-2012_55-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-tcweeklynews-2012-55">\n           [53]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n          <a href="#cite_note-56">\n           [54]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">\n        Demographics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Turks_and_Caicos_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Eight of the thirty islands in the territory are inhabited, with a total population estimated from preliminary results of the census of 25 January 2012 (released on 12 August 2012) of 31,458 inhabitants, an increase of 58.2% from the population of 19,886 reported in the 2001 census.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_3-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-3">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One-third of the population is under 15 years old, and only 4% are 65 or older. In 2000 the population was growing at a rate of 3.55% per year. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">\n        infant mortality\n       </a>\n       rate was 18.66 deaths per 1,000 live births and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">\n        life expectancy\n       </a>\n       at birth was 73.28 years (71.15 years for males, 75.51 years for females). The total fertility rate was 3.25 children born per woman. The annual population growth rate is 2.82%.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The adult population is composed of 57.5% immigrants ("non-belongers"). The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" title="CIA World Factbook">\n        CIA World Factbook\n       </a>\n       describes the islanders\' ethnicity as\n       <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" title="Afro-Caribbean">\n        African\n       </a>\n       87%,\n       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Europe" title="Demographics of Europe">\n        European\n       </a>\n       7.9%,\n       <a href="/wiki/Multiracial" title="Multiracial">\n        Mixed\n       </a>\n       2.5.%,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Caribbean" title="Indo-Caribbean">\n        East Indian\n       </a>\n       1.3% and Other 0.7%\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAPAPUANEWGUINEA_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CIAPAPUANEWGUINEA-57">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vital_statistics">\n        Vital statistics\n
